Refuting spatial distance above the Throne
Nasafi argues that a variable distance above the Throne implies createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming a specific distance above the Throne for Allah leads to the absurd conclusion that the Eternal is originated.

Core Idea
Variable distance requires a specifier; a specifier implies contingency; the Eternal cannot be contingent.

Nasafi presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum against anthropomorphists who claim Allah is at a fixed distance above the Throne. He shows that if such a distance were real, it would be subject to variation, requiring a specifier, and anything that depends on a specifier is originated—a property impossible for the Eternal. This argument reinforces divine transcendence beyond spatial relations.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the logical flow sink in.
Notice how Nasafi uses conditional reasoning.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument begins by noting that the distance could have been less or more. Why is this a problem?
3
Understand the need for a specifier
Since the actual distance is contingent among possibilities, a particularizer (mukhassis) is required. Grasp why this is necessary.
This follows the kalam principle that any contingent determination needs a cause.
4
See how it leads to absurdity
Whatever depends on a specifier is originated (muhdath). Applying originatedness to the Eternal (Qadim) is impossible. Thus the premise of distance is false.
This is a classic reductio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن من الجائز أنه كان أسفل من ذلك فتكون المسافة بينه وبين العرش أقل مما هو الآن أو أعلى من ذلك فتكون تلك المسافة أكثر من ذلك، وليس حدوث المحدثات تتعلق بقدر من أقداره، إذ لا تعلق للعقول بقدر الفاعل وعظمه، وصغره، ولا دلالة فيه على ذلك، فإذا جاز اختصاصه بهذا القدر مع جواز غيره لن يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص، وما يتعلق ثبوته بإثبات غيره إياه كان محدثا، والقول بحدوث القديم محال، والقول به محال .
For it is possible that He was lower than that, so the distance between Him and the Throne would be less than it is now, or higher than that, so that distance would be more than that. And the occurrence of originated things does not depend on a specific measure of His measures, for intellects have no connection to the measure of the agent, His greatness or smallness, nor is there any indication of that in it. So if His specification to this measure is permissible while another is possible, it can only be through the particularization of a particularizer (takhṣīṣ mukhassiṣ). And whatever requires its existence through the affirmation of another thing is originated (muḥdath). And saying that the Eternal (al-Qadīm) is originated is impossible, and saying it is impossible.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage provides a proof against the claim that Allah is at a specific distance above the Throne. Nasafi argues that if Allah were at a certain distance, it would have been possible for Him to be lower or higher, which would change the distance. Since God's state does not change, such variability would require a specifier (mukhassiṣ) that determines the particular distance. Anything that depends on something else for its existence is contingent and originated (muḥdath). Applying originatedness to the Eternal is absurd. Thus the premise that Allah is at a spatial distance is false.

Key Terms
تخصيص مخصص
محال
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God can be at any distance without implying change; Nasafi shows that the possibility of other distances implies a need for specification, which entails createdness.
Correction: The correct understanding is that Allah is not spatially related to the Throne; any fixed distance would require a specifier, making the Eternal originated, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's argument, why does the possibility of different distances above the Throne lead to absurdity?
A) It implies that God is a body.
B) It requires a specifier, which would make God originated.
C) It contradicts the unity of God.
D) It necessitates the existence of two Gods.

Key Takeaway
Allah is not spatially related to the Throne; any fixed distance implies createdness, which is impossible for the Eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you have been imagining Allah in a specific location or direction, how has this affected your worship? Are you willing to abandon that image and submit to the truth that Allah transcends all spatial constraints as this passage demonstrates? Commit to memorizing one phrase from the source that reminds you of this.
?
Nasafi says intellects have no connection to the measure of the agent. Do you sometimes try to measure Allah's attributes by your own standards? How can you guard against this in your daily reflections? Write down one assumption you hold about Allah that may rely on human measurements and resolve to correct it with what you learned here.
?
The argument shows that any fixed distance would require a specifier and thus contingency. Have you ever caught yourself thinking that Allah is 'close' or 'far' in a physical sense? How can you cultivate a sense of nearness that is not spatial but based on faith and obedience? What practical step will you take today to feel His nearness without falling into anthropomorphism?

Allah's Oneness Negates Spatial Location
Nasafi refutes spatial location for Allah using oneness argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the oneness of Allah leads to the logical impossibility of Him being in a place or having spatial location.

Core Idea
If Allah is one, He cannot be in a place without becoming divisible and limited.

Nasafi presents a powerful argument grounded in Allah's unity. The argument begins with a simple premise: a single thing can only occupy one place. From there, he shows how believing Allah is on the Throne or above the world leads to contradictions involving part and whole. This lesson walks through the logical steps and refutes common anthropomorphic misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage once without analyzing. Notice the logical structure: 'if...then...' leading to a conclusion.
The Arabic uses concise logical phrasing.
2
Identify the key premise
The premise 'the one can only occupy one place' is central. Ask: why does oneness imply a single location?
3
Follow the argument to its conclusion
Trace the reasoning: if in a place, then in one part; then similar to that part; impossible. Understand the notion of 'juzʾ lā yatajazzāʾ'.
This part shows the absurdity of spatial location.
4
Consider the specific refutations
See how he applies the same logic to two specific claims: being on the Throne and above the world.
Each refutation uses part-whole reasoning.
5
Reflect on the broader implication
This argument supports Allah's transcendence (tanzih) and refutes anthropomorphism. Think about how it defends tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأنه تعالى شيء واحد، والواحد لا يتمكن إلا في مكان واحد، فلو كان في مكان لكان في جزء واحد ويكون مثلا لذلك الجزء على ما مر فيكون هو تعالى على قدر جزء لا يتجزأ، وهذا محال . (وبطل أيضا قولهم: إنه على العرش لأنه جزء لا يتجزأ من العرش لا يكون عرشا ) وبطل أيضا قولهم: إنه فوق العالم لأن الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ لا يلاقي كل العالم فلا وجه إلى القول بكونه فوق العالم.
And because He, exalted, is one thing, and the one can only occupy one place. So if He were in a place, He would be in a single part and would be similar to that part, as was mentioned, and thus He, exalted, would be according to the measure of a part that is indivisible (juzʾ lā yatajazzāʾ), and this is impossible. And also invalidated is their statement that He is on the Throne, because a part that is indivisible from the Throne is not a Throne. And also invalidated is their statement that He is above the world, because the indivisible part does not contact the whole world, so there is no basis for saying that He is above the world.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents two related arguments against anthropomorphism. First, using God's oneness: a single entity can only be in one place. If God were in a place, He would occupy only one part and would be equal to that indivisible part, which is impossible. Second, Nasafi refutes two specific claims of the anthropomorphists: (1) that God is on the Throne—but if He were on it, He would be a part of it, not the Throne; (2) that God is above the world—an indivisible part cannot be in contact with the whole world. Thus both claims are logically incoherent.

Key Terms
واحد
جزء لا يتجزأ
عرش
فوق العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah literally sits on the Throne or is physically above the world.
Correction: Nasafi shows that such literalism leads to absurdities: it would make Allah a divisible part of creation, contradicting His oneness and transcendence.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi say that being 'on the Throne' would be problematic?
A) Because the Throne is too small.
B) Because it would make God a part of the Throne.
C) Because the Throne is moving.
D) Because God is not a body.

Key Takeaway
Allah's oneness logically entails that He transcends spatial location, making any literal interpretation of being 'on the Throne' or 'above the world' rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may have grown up thinking of Allah as 'above' or 'in heaven'. After reading this lesson, do you realize that such mental images limit Him? How will you actively correct your thoughts when you pray or make du'a?
?
If Allah is not in any place, then there is no 'far' or 'near' in distance. Are there times you treat Allah as distant? What would change in your daily life if you truly felt His closeness without spatial boundaries?
?
The argument shows that Allah's oneness logically excludes location. Where in your heart do you still place Allah—on the Throne, in the sky, or in a sanctuary? Are you willing to let go of that comfortable image and embrace His transcendence, even if it feels less tangible?

Refuting the Karramiyya on God and the Throne
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya claim that God is on the Throne due to greatness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's logical refutation of the Karramiyya claim that God's greatness necessitates spatial specificity to the Throne.

Core Idea
Greatness does not imply spatial multiplicity; circular reasoning invalidates the argument.

The Karramiyya sect attempted to defend the notion that God is specifically on the Throne by appealing to His greatness. Nasafi dissects their argument, showing that 'greatness' is ambiguous and that their explanation becomes circular. This passage demonstrates the importance of precise definitions and logical consistency in theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Follow the Karramiyya's initial objection
Read the beginning where they claim God is with one thing (the Throne) and covers all its parts due to greatness.
Notice the phrase 'مع شيء واحد'.
2
Examine Nasafi's first counter: ambiguity of greatness
Nasafi shows that if greatness means physical bulk, they deny it; if it means majesty, it doesn't confer multiple locations.
3
Identify the circular definition
When they redefine greatness as 'contacting more than one', they use the same phenomenon to explain itself. Nasafi calls this 'جعل الحكم على نفسه'.
See the analogy with 'the world is eternal because it is eternal'.
4
Consider the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi then asks: if greatness allows contact with many things, why not all parts of the world? This would imply God is everywhere in essence, which they reject.
This shows the unlimited nature of greatness leads to pantheism.
5
Conclude with the inevitability of absurdity
The final paragraph declares the doctrine's falsehood is clear to any rational person.
Reflect on the purpose of logical refutations in aqidah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بعض الكرامية الانفصال عن هذا الإلزام فقالوا: إنه تعالى مع شيء واحد فهو على جميع أجزاء العرش وأنه اختص بذلك لعظمته، وهذا هذيان لا طائل تحته، لأنهم إن أرادوا به العظمة من حيث ضخامة الجسم وكثرة الأجزاء فهم لا يقولون به مع أنا أبطلنا القول به، وإن أرادوا به العظمة من حيث الجلال والقدر فالعظمة من هذا الوجه لا توجب اختصاص الموصوف بها بأمكنة كثيرة، فإن السلطان وإن عظم قدره فيما بين العباد لم يختص بمكان هو أكثر أجزاء من ذاته. فإن قالوا: لا نريد بالعظمة ما ذكرتم من الضخامة أو جلال القدر بل نريد به أنه يلاقي أكثر من واحد مع توحد ذاته قيل لهم : هذا الكلام باطل، لأنكم تقولون : إنه مع توحده يلاقي أكثر من واحد لعظمته ثم تفسرون عظمته وتقولون : إن هذه العظمة أنه يلاقي أكثر من واحد مع توحده فيصير حاصل كلامكم أنه مع توحده يلاقي أكثر من واحد، لأنه مع توحده يلاقي أكثر من واحد ، وهذا جعل الحكم عليه لنفسه، ولو جاز ذا لجاز لقائل أن يقول : العالم قديم لأنه قديم، وللعالم صانعان لأنهما صانعان، وغير ذلك، وهذا كله باطل فكذا هذا. ثم يقال لهم: لما جاز أن يلاقي ذات واحد أشياء كثيرة لعظمته لمَ لَمْ يلاق جميع أجزاء العالم فيكون في كل مكان بذاته، ويكون تحت العالم كما كان فوقه؟ وهذا لأنه لا تناهي لعظمته فلا يقتصر على ما بساحة العرش من الأجزاء، وهذا مما لا انفصال لهم عنه. والكلام إذا انتهى إلى مثل هذه المحالات وأفضى المذهب بصاحبه إلى ركوب مثل هذه الترهات لم يبق لذي لب ريبة في بطلانه، ولا لمنصف تردد في فساده، والحمد لله على العصمة.
And some of the Karramiyya attempted to disengage from this objection, so they said: He, exalted, is with one thing, so He is over all the parts of the Throne, and He is specifically so due to His greatness. But this is nonsensical talk with no substance beneath it. For if they mean by greatness the bulkiness of the body and abundance of parts, they do not say that, and we have already invalidated that statement. And if they mean by greatness majesty (jalāl) and power (qadr), then greatness in this sense does not necessitate that the described being is specifically in many places. For the sultan, even if his power is great among subjects, does not specifically occupy a place that has more parts than his essence. If they say: we do not mean by greatness what you mentioned of bulk or majesty of power, but we mean by it that He contacts more than one while His essence is one, it is said to them: this speech is false, because you say: He, with His oneness, contacts more than one due to His greatness, then you interpret His greatness and say: this greatness is that He contacts more than one with His oneness. So the conclusion of your speech becomes: He, with His oneness, contacts more than one because He, with His oneness, contacts more than one. And this is making the judgment dependent on itself. And if this were permissible, it would be permissible for someone to say: the world is eternal (qadīm) because it is eternal, and the world has two creators because they are two creators, and so on. And all this is false, so likewise this. Then it is said to them: Since it is permissible for one essence to contact many things due to its greatness, why does it not contact all parts of the world, so that it would be in every place by its essence, and be under the world as it was above it? And this is because there is no limit to its greatness, so it is not restricted to the parts in the area of the Throne. And this is something they cannot disengage from. And when speech reaches such impossibilities and the doctrine leads its adherent to mounting such absurdities, no one with intellect remains in doubt about its falsehood, nor does any fair person hesitate about its corruption. And praise be to Allah for protection.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyya objection. They claimed that God is on the Throne because He is with one thing (the Throne) but covers all its parts due to His greatness. Nasafi first points out that 'greatness' (ʿaẓama) is ambiguous: if it means physical bulk, they deny that; if it means majesty, that does not grant multiple locations. When they redefine greatness as 'contacting more than one while being one', Nasafi exposes the circular reasoning: they explain greatness by the very phenomenon it is supposed to explain. He gives an analogy: saying 'the world is eternal because it is eternal' is equally circular. Then he pushes the absurdity further: if greatness allows contact with many things, why not all parts of the world? Since greatness is limitless, it should apply everywhere, leading to pantheism. The conclusion is that the entire doctrine collapses into absurdity, leaving no doubt of its falsehood.

Key Terms
الكرامية
عظمة
هذيان
جعل الحكم على نفسه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think God's greatness allows spatial multiplicity, so He can be specifically on the Throne.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this leads to circular definitions and unlimited extension, which are absurd. Greatness in the sense of majesty does not imply multiple locations.

Checkpoint
What logical error does Nasafi identify in the Karramiyya definition of 'greatness'?
A) It contradicts the Quran.
B) It is a circular definition that explains the phenomenon by itself.
C) It is too vague.
D) It implies God is a body.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's refutation demonstrates that theological claims must be logically coherent and free from circular reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God without examining whether the reasons you give for it are actually circular? Think of one belief you hold about God's attributes. Can you explain why you hold that belief without using the belief itself as evidence? If you cannot, then what does that say about your certainty?
?
Nasafi shows that even a seemingly pious claim (that God's greatness puts Him on the Throne) can be absurd if not logically sound. What is one area of your faith where you might be relying on a comfortable but unexamined explanation? Are you willing to subject it to the same scrutiny Nasafi applies here?
?
The Karramiyya redefined greatness to save their argument. When you find your beliefs challenged, do you tend to adjust definitions to protect your position, or do you humbly accept correction? Give an honest example from your own life.

Argument from Limited Direction to All Directions
Nasafi's reductio against directionality of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's reductio argument that if Allah can be limited to one direction, then He must be limited to all directions, leading to an absurdity.

Core Idea
If Allah can be in one direction, there is no reason to exclude any direction.

Nasafi presents a powerful logical argument against those who claim Allah occupies a specific direction. He shows that if spatial limitation is possible at all, then there is no rational basis to restrict it to one direction — but this leads to an impossible conclusion. Let's examine the reasoning carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm, then read the English translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'since it is permissible... it becomes permissible...'
The passage is cut off, but the essential argument is complete.
2
Identify the key premise
Nasafi starts from the opponent's own claim: that Allah is limited to a specific direction (e.g., above). He then asks: what makes this direction special?
He uses the phrase 'لا دليل يوجب التفرقة بين جهة وجهة' (no proof necessitates differentiation).
3
Follow the logical chain
If there is no distinction between directions, then what is permissible in one direction is permissible in all. This leads to the conclusion that Allah could be limited in all directions simultaneously, which is absurd.
The argument shows that the original premise (directionality) is false because it leads to an impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول لهم : لما جاز أن يكون محدودا بجهة جاز أن يكون محدودا بجميع الجهات إذ لا دليل يوجب التفرقة بين جهة وجهة إذ لما جاز الاختصاص على هذا القدر من هذه الجهة جاز على غيرها من الجهات لأن جوازه من هذه الجهة دلیل جوازه على القديم فلم يمتنع عنه جميع الجهات، وإذا جاز هذا ثُمَّ جاز أن ...
Then we say to them: Since it is permissible that He be limited (maḥdūd) by a direction, it becomes permissible that He be limited by all directions, for there is no proof that necessitates differentiation between one direction and another. Since specification to this measure from this direction is permissible, it is permissible from other directions, because its permissibility from this direction indicates its permissibility regarding the Eternal, so all directions are not impossible for Him. And when this is permissible, then it is permissible that ...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a final argument against those who claim Allah is in a specific direction (e.g., above the Throne). Nasafi uses a reductio: if it is allowed that Allah be limited to one direction (such as 'above'), then there is no reason to differentiate between directions. What makes one direction permissible should make all directions permissible. This would mean Allah could be limited in all directions simultaneously, which is absurd. The argument shows that the original premise (that Allah is in a direction) is false because it leads to an impossibility. The text trails off, but the argument's conclusion is clear: such a position is untenable.

Key Terms
محدود
جهة
تفرقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Allah can be in one direction (e.g., above) without entailing other directions.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if spatial limitation is possible at all, there is no rational basis to restrict it to one direction; thus the claim leads to absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's argument, if it is permissible for God to be in one direction, why must all directions be permissible?
A) Because God is infinite.
B) Because there is no logical basis to differentiate between directions.
C) Because the Throne exists in all directions.
D) Because God's power necessitates covering all directions.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument shows that claiming Allah is in any direction logically leads to absurdity, affirming His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you raise your hands for du'a, do you unconsciously imagine Allah as being in a certain direction? Nasafi's argument shows that any direction is a limitation. How will you train your heart to feel His nearness without spatial imagining?
?
If Allah is beyond all directions, then He is equally close to you everywhere—even in moments of sin or distraction. Does that comfort you or unsettle you? How should it change your awareness of His presence right now?
?
The argument destroys the idea that Allah is 'above' in a literal sense. When you recite verses about the Throne, how will you now conceive of His majesty without falling into direction? What specific mental shift is required of you?

Nasafi's Reductio on Directionality
Nasafi's reductio argument against directionality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's reductio argument against directionality for God, showing how it leads to the absurdity of created bodies encompassing Him.

Core Idea
Directionality reduces God to a pearl in a pocket.

Nasafi presents a devastating reductio argument: if God could be in one direction, there is no reason to exclude all directions. This leads to the absurd conclusion that created bodies could encompass Him, likening Him to a tiny pearl. This lesson traces his logical steps and reveals why the original assumption is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the concise logical progression.
The argument is a single continuous reductio.
2
Identify the premise
The opponent's premise: it is permissible for God to be limited to one direction.
Nasafi does not accept this; he is showing its consequences.
3
Follow the logical chain
From one direction, no distinction leads to all directions being permissible. Then created bodies could meet Him from all sides.
This is the key inference.
4
See the absurd consequence
Bodies would encompass God like a pearl that can be held in a hand or placed in a pocket.
This is clearly absurd for the Creator.
5
Understand the reductio
Since the consequence is disbelief and nonsense, the original premise must be false. Nasafi defends divine transcendence.
This argument preserves tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول لهم : لما جاز أن يكون محدودا بجهة جاز أن يكون محدودا بجميع الجهات إذ لا دليل يوجب التفرقة بين جهة وجهة إذ لما جاز الاختصاص على هذا القدر من هذه الجهة جاز على غيرها من الجهات لأن جوازه من هذه الجهة دلیل جوازه على القديم فلم يمتنع عنه جميع الجهات، وإذا جاز هذا ثُمَّ جاز أن يلاقيه الأجسام المحدثة من هذا الجانب جاز أيضا من تلك الجهات، ولو جاز ذا لأحاطت به الأجسام إحاطة ألحقته باللؤلؤ، ثم ما من قدر له ولما يحيط به إلا وما هو دونه، وأصغر منه من جملة الجائزات فيؤول الأمر إلى أن يجوز أن يكون مثل لؤلؤة في حقه صغيرة يأخذها الإنسان بيده ويضعها في صندوق أو في جيبه وكل ذلك كفر وهذيان، فكذا ما أدى إليه وبالله العصمة والنجاة من كل ضلال وبدعة.
Then we say to them: Since it is permissible that He be limited to one direction, it is permissible that He be limited to all directions, since there is no evidence that necessitates distinction between one direction and another. For since specification to this extent in this direction is permissible, it is permissible in other directions, because its permissibility from this direction is evidence of its permissibility for the Eternal. So none of the directions are prevented from Him. And if this is permissible, then it is permissible that the originated bodies meet Him from this side, and also from those directions. And if this were permissible, then bodies would encompass Him with an encompassing that would liken Him to a pearl. Then there is no extent for Him and for what encompasses Him except that it is below Him and smaller than Him among possible things. So the matter results in it being permissible that He be like a small pearl in His regard, that a human takes in his hand and places in a box or in his pocket. And all of that is disbelief and nonsense. So likewise what leads to it. And by God is protection and deliverance from every error and innovation.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage argues that accepting directionality leads to absurdities. The author posits: if God can be confined to one direction, there is no evidence to forbid all directions. The same permissibility applies universally, because once specification to one direction is allowed, it sets a precedent for any direction. If God is approachable from all sides, then originated bodies (الأجسام المحدثة) could meet Him from every side, thereby encompassing Him. This encompassing would liken Him to a pearl—a finite object that can be held in a hand, placed in a box or pocket. Such a conception is disbelief (كفر) and nonsense (هذيان). Therefore, the original assumption (that God is in a direction) is false, and what leads to it is likewise false. The author concludes by seeking God's protection from all error and innovation.

Key Terms
محدود بجهة
إحاطة
لؤلؤة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is harmless to say God is in a direction.
Correction: Nasafi shows this leads to the absurdity of God being encompassed by created bodies like a pearl, which is disbelief.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does Nasafi derive from allowing God to be limited to all directions?
A) God becomes invisible
B) Created bodies could encompass Him like a pearl
C) God would have no attributes
D) The world would be eternal

Key Takeaway
Accepting any direction for God leads to the absurd conclusion that He can be encompassed by created bodies, which is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believed God is in a specific direction, what would stop you from eventually reducing Him to a finite object? How does this lesson expose the danger of even a single direction?
?
The argument shows that any limitation on God leads to absurdity. In what areas of your life do you subconsciously try to limit God—by expecting Him to act in a certain way or fit into your plans? What would it mean to let go of that limitation?
?
Nasafi says that allowing directionality reduces God to a pearl in a pocket. When you imagine God, do you have an unconscious image or direction? What practical steps can you take to purify your conception of God from all mental images?

Refutation of 'God Fills the Throne Area'
Nasafi refutes the claim that God fills the Throne area with a logical reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a logical reductio to refute the claim that God exactly fills the area of the Throne, demonstrating that such a view implies divine limitation and impossibility.

Core Idea
Attributing location to Allah implies limitation, which is impossible for the Creator.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a specific anthropomorphic view—the claim that Allah exactly fills the area of the Throne without exceeding it. He shows that this claim necessarily concedes that Allah has limits (حد ونهاية), because the Throne itself is finite. Then, through a series of logical questions, he forces the opponent into absurd conclusions about Allah's power and the possibility of creation encompassing Him. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the translation. Notice the conditional structure (if... then...) used in the refutation.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The passage begins by stating the view being refuted: that God 'filled the area of the Throne and did not exceed it.' Understand why this implies limit and end from all sides.
The Throne is finite (متناه), so the view places Allah within finite boundaries.
3
Trace the first reductio (increasing the Throne)
Nasafi asks: Can God increase the Throne from all sides? Consider the two possible answers: 'No' implies incapability; 'Yes' makes God smaller than the enlarged Throne.
Both answers lead to impossibilities regarding God's perfection.
4
Trace the second reductio (folding the Throne's parts)
Then he asks: Can God fold the excess parts of the Throne to encompass Himself? Again, 'No' implies incapability; 'Yes' means created things encompass Him.
This final outcome is absurd, so the original claim is invalid.
5
Summarize the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that the opponent has affirmed the permissibility of created things encompassing Allah—an impossibility. Thus, the view that God fills the Throne is refuted.
This reinforces the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا هذا على قول من يقول : إنه ملأ ساحة العرش، ولم يفضل منها. بل أولى لأنه يسلم له الحد والنهاية من الجوانب الأربع حيث زعم أنه لا يفضل ساحة العرش والعرش متناه، وكذا يقال له: أيقدر أن يزيد في العرش من الجوانب كلها؟ فإن قال : لا . فقد عجزه، وإن قال: نعم، قيل : فإذا زيد فيه صار أصغر من العرش. فهل يقدر أن يعطف ما فضل منه من أجزاء العرش على جوانبه فيحيط به؟ فإن قال: لا. فقد عجزه. وإن قال: نعم فقد أثبت ما ألزمنا من جواز إحاطة المخلوقات به والله الموفق.
And similarly this applies to the one who says: He filled the area of the Throne and did not exceed it. Rather it is more fitting, because he concedes limit and end from the four sides, since he claims that He does not exceed the area of the Throne, while the Throne is finite. And similarly it is said to him: Is He able to increase the Throne from all sides? If he says: No, then he has rendered Him incapable. And if he says: Yes, it is said: So if it is increased, He becomes smaller than the Throne. Then is He able to fold what has exceeded of the parts of the Throne over its sides so that it encompasses Him? If he says: No, then he has rendered Him incapable. And if he says: Yes, then he has affirmed what we have forced upon him of the permissibility of the created things encompassing Him. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific form of directionalism: the claim that God exactly fills the throne area without exceeding it. The author notes that this view concedes that God has limits (حد ونهاية) from all four sides, because the Throne is finite (متناه). He then uses a series of questions to expose the absurdity. First, he asks whether God can increase the Throne on all sides. If the opponent says no, then God is incapable (عجزه). If yes, then when the Throne is enlarged, God becomes smaller relative to it. Then, can God fold the excess parts of the Throne around Himself so that they encompass Him? If no, again incapability. If yes, then He admits that created things can encompass God—an absurd conclusion. Thus, the position collapses.

Key Terms
ملأ ساحة العرش
حد ونهاية
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that Allah exactly fills the area of the Throne without excess is acceptable because it only says He is in a specific location.
Correction: This belief implies that Allah has limits and is contained by a created object (the Throne), which contradicts His transcendence and perfection. Nasafi's argument shows the logical absurdities that follow from such a view.

Checkpoint
In the argument against the one who says God fills the Throne area, what does Nasafi ask about increasing the Throne?
A) To show God's power
B) To show that God would become smaller if the Throne is enlarged
C) To prove the Throne is eternal
D) To assert that God does not fill it

Key Takeaway
The claim that Allah fills the Throne area leads to attributing limitations to Allah, which is impossible; this passage refutes such anthropomorphism through logical reductio.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah as occupying a space, even unconsciously? How does this passage challenge you to purify your conception of Allah, and what concrete step can you take today to replace that mental image with a correct one?

This argument shows that even well-intentioned reverence (like saying Allah fills the Throne) can lead to absurd conclusions about Allah. Are there any beliefs or practices you hold about Allah that, when logically examined, might imply limitation or imperfection? Will you commit to seeking knowledge to correct them?
?
The opponents in this passage were presumably trying to exalt Allah, yet their claim led to attributing incapability to Him. In your own worship or speech about Allah, where might you be unintentionally limiting Him? How can you use the logical method of this passage to check your own understanding?

Conclusion: Nasafi Rejects Two False Views on Allah's Location
Nasafi concludes that both directionalism and indwelling are false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both the view that Allah is in a specific place and the view that He is everywhere by His essence are false according to Nasafi's conclusion.

Core Idea
Allah transcends both confinement to a place and indwelling in all places.

Nasafi has presented arguments demonstrating the absurdity of two extreme positions on Allah's location. In this concluding passage, he summarises that both views are clearly false, warning against the theological errors that follow from each.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the conclusion Nasafi draws.
Notice the repeated 'ظهر بطلان' indicating two falsehoods.
2
Identify the two rejected views
Find the two positions Nasafi declares false: (1) God in a specific place or direction, (2) God everywhere by essence.
Both are rejected; they are opposite extremes.
3
Understand the consequence of the second view
Nasafi argues that if God is everywhere by essence, He would be divided, impure - an absurdity.
This shows why panentheism is false.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Consider how both errors arise from trying to locate Allah. The correct belief is that He transcends space and direction altogether.
This is the core tawhid lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالوقف على هذه الجملة ظهر بطلان قول من قال إنه تعالى في مكان دون مكان، أو في جهة من الجهات، وظهر أيضا بطلان قول من قال: إنه تعالى بكل مكان ذاته لأنه يلزمه أنه متبعض متجزئ يلاقي كل جزء من أجزاء العالم جزءً منه، ويلزمه أن يكون في أجواف الحيوانات، وآبار الكنيف، ومواضع الأقذار والأنتان، وهذا كله ظاهر البطلان.
And by stopping at these statements, the falsehood of the statement of those who say that He, exalted is He, is in a specific place rather than another, or in one of the directions, becomes manifest. And also the falsehood of the statement of those who say that He, exalted is He, is in every place by His essence becomes manifest, because it entails that He is divided and partitioned, that a part of Him meets every part of the world, and that He be in the insides of animals, and the pits of the privy, and places of filth and stench. And all of this is clearly false.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage serves as a conclusion to the preceding arguments. The author states that by 'stopping at these statements' (بالوقف على هذه الجملة)—referring to the absurd consequences drawn—the falsehood of two extreme views becomes manifest. The first view is that God is in a specific place or direction (في مكان دون مكان أو في جهة من الجهات). The second view is that God is everywhere by His essence (بكل مكان ذاته). The latter is false because it implies that God is divided and partitioned (متبعض متجزئ), with a part of Him meeting every part of the world, leading to the blasphemous conclusion that He would be present in impure places like animal insides, latrine pits, and areas of filth. Both views are clearly false.

Key Terms
مكان دون مكان
بكل مكان ذاته
متبعض متجزئ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Allah is physically in a specific place (e.g., the Throne) or that He is physically everywhere by His essence.
Correction: Allah is not confined to any place nor distributed throughout creation; He is transcendent and not subject to spatial limitations.

Checkpoint

A) God is in a specific place and God is everywhere by knowledge
B) God is in a specific place and God is everywhere by essence
C) God is everywhere by essence and God is nowhere
D) God is in the Throne and God is in the heart

Key Takeaway
Both directionalism and panentheism (God in all places by essence) are false because they contradict Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you willing to let go of any comfortable but incorrect notion of God's presence, even if it feels less intimate? What step will you take today to align your heart with the truth of His transcendence?

Refutation of Divine Location and Direction
Nasafi refutes claims that God is in a place or direction using absurd consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claims that Allah is in a specific place, direction, or everywhere by essence are rationally impossible.

Core Idea
If Allah could be located, He could be contained—and that is absurd.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi deploys a series of logical reductions (reductio ad absurdum) to dismantle any notion that Allah occupies space or is subject to direction. By assuming the opponent's premises, he shows they lead to conclusions that are both blasphemous and rationally contradictory. The following commentary will walk you through each step of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the use of hypothetical reasoning: 'if this were permissible...'
2
Understand the pearl analogy
Focus on the first part of the passage where Nasafi imagines bodies surrounding Allah like a pearl. Ask: why is this analogy absurd?
The pearl can be held in a hand—this implies utter finitude.
3
Follow the Throne-filling dilemma
Examine the second argument about Allah filling the Throne courtyard. Trace the dilemma about increasing the Throne and its consequences.
This shows that any notion of limit leads to contradiction.
4
Reflect on the final conclusion
Read the concluding lines about the invalidity of both 'specific place' and 'everywhere by essence' claims. Consider why the latter leads to partition and impurity.
The refutation is comprehensive: it covers both extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يلاقيه الأجسام المحدثة من هذا الجانب جاز أيضا من تلك الجهات، ولو جاز ذا لأحاطت به الأجسام إحاطة ألحقته باللؤلؤ، ثم ما من قدر له ولما يحيط به إلا وما هو دونه، وأصغر منه من جملة الجائزات فيؤول الأمر إلى أن يجوز أن يكون مثل لؤلؤة في حقه صغيرة يأخذها الإنسان بيده ويضعها في صندوق أو في جيبه وكل ذلك كفر وهذيان، فكذا ما أدى إليه وبالله العصمة والنجاة من كل ضلال وبدعة. وكذا هذا على قول من يقول : إنه ملأ ساحة العرش، ولم يفضل منها. بل أولى لأنه يسلم له الحد والنهاية من الجوانب الأربع حيث زعم أنه لا يفضل ساحة العرش والعرش متناه، وكذا يقال له: أيقدر أن يزيد في العرش من الجوانب كلها؟ فإن قال : لا . فقد عجزه، وإن قال: نعم، قيل : فإذا زيد فيه صار أصغر من العرش. فهل يقدر أن يعطف ما فضل منه من أجزاء العرش على جوانبه فيحيط به؟ فإن قال: لا. فقد عجزه. وإن قال : نعم فقد أثبت ما ألزمنا من جواز إحاطة المخلوقات به والله الموفق.
وبالوقف على هذه الجملة ظهر بطلان قول من قال إنه تعالى في مكان دون مكان، أو في جهة من الجهات، وظهر أيضا بطلان قول من قال: إنه تعالى بكل مكان ذاته لأنه يلزمه أنه متبعض متجزئ يلاقي كل جزء من أجزاء العالم جزءً منه، ويلزمه أن يكون في أجواف الحيوانات، وآبار الكنيف، ومواضع الأقذار والأنتان، وهذا كله ظاهر البطلان.
The originated bodies meet Him from this side, [then] it would also be permissible from those directions. And if this were permissible, the bodies would surround Him with a surrounding that would liken Him to a pearl. Then there is no extent for Him and for what surrounds Him except that it is less than Him, and smaller than Him, out of the class of possibilities. So the matter leads to [the possibility] that He would be like a small pearl in His regard, which a person takes in his hand and puts in a box or in his pocket; all of that is disbelief and nonsense. Likewise, whatever leads to it [is the same]. And with Allah is protection and deliverance from every misguidance and innovation. And likewise this [applies] to the saying of one who says: He filled the courtyard of the Throne, and nothing remained of it. Rather it is more fitting, because he concedes limit and termination from the four sides, since he claims that nothing remains of the courtyard of the Throne, and the Throne is finite. And likewise it is said to him: Is He able to increase the Throne from all sides? If he says: No, then he has rendered Him incapable. If he says: Yes, it is said: Then if it is increased, He becomes smaller than the Throne. Then is He able to fold what remained of the parts of the Throne around its sides and surround Him? If he says: No, then he has rendered Him incapable. If he says: Yes, then he has affirmed what we compelled him [to accept] of the permissibility of the creatures surrounding Him. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And by pausing at this summary, the invalidity appears of the saying of one who says that He, exalted, is in a place rather than another place, or in a direction among directions. And also appears the invalidity of the saying of one who says: He, exalted, is in every place by His essence, because it necessitates that He is partitioned and divided, each part of the world meeting a part of Him, and it necessitates that He be in the insides of animals, in the wells of privies, and in places of filth and stench. And all of this is clearly invalid.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a reductio ad absurdum argument against those who claim that God is in a specific place or direction. The author begins by assuming the opponent's position: if God were in a direction, then created bodies could meet Him from that side. By extension, they could meet Him from all sides, leading to the conclusion that bodies would surround Him, likening Him to a pearl that can be held in a hand or placed in a box. This is blasphemous nonsense. The same reasoning applies to the claim that God fills the area of the Throne without exceeding it; this concedes limitation and boundary. The author then poses a dilemma: if the Throne were increased, God would become smaller than it, or if not, God is incapable. Either way, the opponent's position leads to absurdity. After this, the author concludes that such arguments invalidate both the statement that God is in a specific place/direction and the statement that He is in every place by His essence, since the latter entails partition and contamination—clearly impossible for God.

Key Terms
جهة
مكان
العرش
إحاطة
اللؤلؤة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God being 'with' His creation or 'above' the Throne implies physical containment or location.
Correction: Allah's attributes of being with creation or above the Throne are not physical; they are transcendent and beyond spatial limitations.

Checkpoint
What does the pearl analogy illustrate?
A) That God is like a pearl in value.
B) That if God were in a direction, He could be physically surrounded and handled, an absurdity.
C) That God's essence is everywhere.
D) That God is limited to the Throne.

Key Takeaway
Allah is utterly transcendent; any claim of physical location or containment leads to logical absurdity and is contrary to tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray facing the qibla, do you ever catch yourself imagining Allah physically in that direction? How does Nasafi's pearl analogy expose the irrationality of that thought?
?
If you honestly reflect, are there hidden assumptions in your heart that Allah is 'somewhere'—in the heavens, above the Throne, or in a particular place? What would it mean for your tawhid if you allowed those assumptions to remain?
?
The passage says such beliefs lead to 'disbelief and nonsense.' Have you ever considered the logical consequences of attributing location to Allah? Are you willing to uproot any subtle anthropomorphic thoughts, even if they feel comforting, to protect your belief in His absolute transcendence?

The False Claim of Deficiency in Direction
Nasafi refutes the idea that direction implies deficiency and traps the opponent with a substance dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the claim that having a direction implies deficiency, and see the trap regarding substance.

Core Idea
Direction is not deficient; deficiency depends on context.

In this lesson, we begin with Nasafi's initial counter-arguments against the idea that direction (jiha) is inherently deficient. He gives everyday examples to show that being above or below is not blameworthy per se. He then poses a dilemma about substances to expose a flaw in the opponent's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the opponent's claim
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. The opponent claims direction is deficiency.
2
Notice Nasafi's examples
He gives examples of a guard on a roof and an emir in a house. Why do these refute deficiency?
Direction is neutral; honor depends on role, not location.
3
See the dilemma about substance
Nasafi asks: if they say God is a substance, they contradict their own doctrine; if they deny it, their analogy fails.
This sets up the need for a proper rule of analogy.
4
Reflect on the argument
Ask yourself how this initial refutation prepares for the next lessons on transference and direction.
Connects to learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواز ذلك على الشاهد فلم قلتم إن دليل التفرقة فيما نحن فيه لم يوجد؟ بل وجد أنه يوجب الحدوث وهو ممتنع على الغائب جائز بل واجب على الشاهد. ثم نقول لهم: كون جهة تحت جهة ذم ونقيصة غير مسلم إذ لا نقيصة في ذلك ولا رفعة في علو المكان، إذ كم من حارس فوق السطح وأمير في البيت وطليعة على ما ارتفع من الأماكن وسلطان في ما انهبط من الأمكنة. ثم نقول لهم: كل قائم بالذات في الشاهد جوهر وكل جوهر قائم بالذات أفتستدلون بذلك على أن الغائب جوهر؟ فإن قالوا: نعم. فقد تركوا مذهبهم ووافقوا النصارى، وإن قالوا: لا. نقضوا دليلهم. ثم نقول لهم: إنما يجب التعدية من الشاهد إلى الغائب إذا تعلق أحد الأمرين بالآخر تعلق العلة بالمعلول، كما في العلم والعالم، والحركة والمتحرك، وذلك مما لا يقتصر على مجرد الوجود، بل يشترط فيه زيادة شرط، وهو أن يستحيل إضافته إلى غيره، ألا ترى أن العالم كما لا ينفك عن العلم والعلم عن العالم، يستحيل إضافة كونه عالما إلى شيء وراء العلم. فعلم أنه كان عالما لأن له علما فوجبت التعدية إلى الغائب والجوهرية مع القيام بالذات إن كان لا ينفكان في الشاهد ولكن لما لم يكن جوهرا لقيامه بالذات بل لكونه أصلا يتركب منه الجسم لم يجب تعدية كونه جوهرا يتعدى كونه قائما بالذات وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فلم قلتم: إنهما كانا في الشاهد موجودين قائمين بالذات لأن كل واحد منهما بجهة من صاحبه أو كان كل واحد منهما بجهة صاحبه لأنهما موجودان قائمان بالذات. ثم نقول لهم: لو كانا موجودين قائمين بالذات لأن كل واحد منهما بجهة من صاحبه، لكان الموجود القائم بالذات بالجهة وإن لم يكن معه غيره، ولكان الباري جل وعلا في الأزل بجهة، لأنه كان موجودا قائما بالذات وهذا محال، إذ الجهة لا تثبت إلا باعتبار غير، ألا ترى أن الجهات كلها محصورة على الست وهي فوق وتحت وخلف وقدام وعن يمين وعن يسار، وكل جهة منها لن يتصور ثبوتها إلا بمقابلة غيرها، والكل يتركب من الفرد، فإذا كان كل فرد من الجهات لن يتصور إلا بين اثنين، فكان حكم كلية الجهات كذلك، لما مر من حصول المعرفة بالكليات اسطة الجزئيات، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك كان تعليق الجهة بالوجود والقيام بالذات مع أن كل واحد منهما يثبت باعتبار النفس دون الغير، والجهة لا تثبت إلا باعتبار الغير جهلا بالحقائق. ثم يقال لهم: أتزعمون أن القائمين بالذات يكون كل واحد منهما بجهة من صاحبه على الإطلاق بشريطة كون كل واحد منهما محدودا متناهيا؟ فإن قالوا: على الإطلاق. فلا نسلم وما استدلوا به من الشاهد فهما محدودان متناهيان. وإن قالوا نقول ذلك بشريطة كون كل واحد منهما محدودا متناهيا. فمسلم. ولكن لم قلتم إن الباري محدد متناه؟ ثم إنا قد أقمنا الدلالة على استحالة كونه محدودا متناهيا. والله الموفق.
And [the] permissibility of that in the witnessed world – so why did you say that the evidence of distinction in our case does not exist? Rather it exists: it necessitates origination, which is impossible for the unseen, but permissible and even obligatory for the witnessed. Then we say to them: [the claim that] being under or above a direction is blame and deficiency is not conceded, for there is no deficiency in that nor elevation in highness of place, for how many a guard is above the roof and an emir in the house and a scout on elevated places and a sultan in low places. Then we say to them: every self-subsistent in the witnessed is a substance, and every substance is self-subsistent – do you then infer from that that the unseen is a substance? If they say: yes, then they have abandoned their doctrine and agreed with the Christians; and if they say: no, they have invalidated their evidence. Then we say to them: transference from the witnessed to the unseen is only obligatory when one of the two things is connected to the other with the connection of cause to effect, as in knowledge and the knower, and motion and the moving thing; and that does not rely merely on existence, but requires an additional condition, namely that it is impossible to attribute it to another. Do you not see that just as the knower is inseparable from knowledge and knowledge from the knower, it is impossible to attribute his being knowing to something beyond knowledge. So it is known that he was knowing because he has knowledge, so transference to the unseen is obligatory. But substantiality together with self-subsistence – if they are inseparable in the witnessed, but since it is not a substance because of its self-subsistence, but because it is a root from which the body is composed, the transference of its being a substance is not obligatory; rather the transference of its being self-subsistent is transitive. And when the matter is so, why did you say: the two of them in the witnessed exist, self-subsistent, because each one of them is in a direction from its companion, or each one of them is in the direction of its companion because they exist and are self-subsistent? Then we say to them: if they existed and were self-subsistent because each one of them is in a direction from its companion, then the existent self-subsistent would be in a direction even if there were no other with it, and the Creator, Exalted and High, would have been in a direction in pre-eternity because He was existent and self-subsistent – and this is impossible. For direction is only established by consideration of another. Do you not see that all directions are limited to six: above, below, behind, front, right, left; and each direction cannot be imagined to be established except by facing another; and the whole is composed of the individual; so when each individual direction cannot be imagined except between two, the rule of all direction is likewise, because of what has passed about obtaining knowledge of universals through the particular. And when the matter is so, attributing direction to existence and self-subsistence – while each of them is established by consideration of the self, not the other, and direction is only established by consideration of the other – is ignorance of realities. Then it is said to them: do you claim that self-subsistents are each in a direction from its companion absolutely, with the condition that each of them is limited and finite? If they say: absolutely – we do not concede; and what they adduce from the witnessed, both are limited and finite. And if they say: we say that with the condition that each of them is limited and finite – then it is conceded. But why do you say that the Creator is limited and finite? Moreover, we have already established proof of the impossibility of His being limited and finite. And God is the success.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument that attempts to prove that God has a direction (jiha) based on analogy (tamthil) from the witnessed world (shahid). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, presents several responses to this claim. First, he challenges the premise that direction implies deficiency, giving examples from everyday life where being above or below is not inherently deficient. Second, he questions the analogy by asking whether the opponent infers that God is a substance (jawhar) because all self-subsistent beings in the witnessed world are substances. If they say yes, they contradict their own doctrine and agree with Christians (who hold that God is a substance). If they say no, their analogy fails. Third, he explains the proper conditions for transference (ta'diya) from the witnessed to the unseen: it requires a necessary connection like cause and effect, not mere coexistence. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-dhat) does not necessarily entail direction, as direction requires another entity. Fourth, he argues that if self-subsistence implied direction, then God would have been in a direction in pre-eternity (before creation), which is impossible because direction presupposes a relation to something else. He then analyzes the nature of directions (above, below, etc.) showing that each requires a counterpart, so direction cannot be an intrinsic attribute of a self-subsistent being. Finally, he presents a conditional objection: if the opponent says the analogy holds only for limited and finite beings, then we concede but ask why they claim God is limited and finite, since that has been proven impossible.

Key Terms
جهة
شاهد
غائب
جوهر
قيام بالذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because bodies in the world have directions, God must also have a direction to be real.
Correction: Nasafi shows that direction is relative and not an essential attribute; transference requires more than shared existence.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the consequence if the opponent says that God is a substance?
A) God would be limited and finite.
B) They would have contradicted their own doctrine and agreed with Christians.
C) Their analogy would be valid.
D) God would be in a direction.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the idea that direction implies deficiency and exposes the flawed analogy about substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever secretly imagine God as 'above' in a spatial sense, and then attribute to that direction a sense of honor or majesty? How does Nasafi's example of the emir and guard challenge your mental picture of God's transcendence? Tonight, when you pray, consciously reject any spatial or directional image of God—how does that feel?
?
The opponents in this passage insisted on their analogy despite its contradictions. Are there any analogies you have been clinging to in your understanding of God—perhaps from your upbringing or from human relationships—that might actually be forms of covert tashbih? What would it cost you to abandon them?
?
Nasafi's dilemma forces a stark choice: either reduce God to a substance or reject the entire analogy. Are you willing to reject any analogy that fails to preserve God's absolute uniqueness, even if it means leaving some questions unanswered? What is the one belief about God that you find hardest to let go of because it makes God feel closer or more relatable?

Divine Transcendence

5 min
The Proper Rule of Transference (Ta'diya)
Nasafi defines the condition for valid transference from witnessed to unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's principle that transference from the witnessed to the unseen requires a cause-effect relationship, not mere shared attributes.

Core Idea
Analogy needs necessary connection, not just coexistence.

In the previous lesson, we saw the trap about substance. Now Nasafi lays down the proper method for moving from the witnessed to the unseen: it must be based on a necessary connection like cause and effect. He uses the example of knowledge and the knower.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key condition
Read the Arabic and translation. The key condition is 't'alluq al-'illa bil-ma'lul' (connection of cause to effect).
2
Understand the example of knowledge and knower
Knowledge and knower are inseparable; knowledge is the cause of being knower. This allows transference.
This is a valid analogy.
3
See how this applies to substance
Substantiality is not caused by self-subsistence but by being a root of body—so no transference.
4
Connect to direction
Nasafi asks why they think self-subsistence implies direction—there is no cause-effect link.

Source Text

وجواز ذلك على الشاهد فلم قلتم إن دليل التفرقة فيما نحن فيه لم يوجد؟ بل وجد أنه يوجب الحدوث وهو ممتنع على الغائب جائز بل واجب على الشاهد. ثم نقول لهم: كون جهة تحت جهة ذم ونقيصة غير مسلم إذ لا نقيصة في ذلك ولا رفعة في علو المكان، إذ كم من حارس فوق السطح وأمير في البيت وطليعة على ما ارتفع من الأماكن وسلطان في ما انهبط من الأمكنة. ثم نقول لهم: كل قائم بالذات في الشاهد جوهر وكل جوهر قائم بالذات أفتستدلون بذلك على أن الغائب جوهر؟ فإن قالوا: نعم. فقد تركوا مذهبهم ووافقوا النصارى، وإن قالوا: لا. نقضوا دليلهم. ثم نقول لهم: إنما يجب التعدية من الشاهد إلى الغائب إذا تعلق أحد الأمرين بالآخر تعلق Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument that attempts to prove that God has a direction (jiha) based on analogy (tamthil) from the witnessed world (shahid). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, presents several responses to this claim. First, he challenges the premise that direction implies deficiency, giving examples from everyday life where being above or below is not inherently deficient. Second, he questions the analogy by asking whether the opponent infers that God is a substance (jawhar) because all self-subsistent beings in the witnessed world are substances. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any attribute common in witnessed can be transferred to God.

According to Nasafi, what condition must be met for valid transference (ta'diya) from the witnessed to the unseen?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself assuming that because something is true of created things (like being in a direction), it must also be true of God? How does this passage call you to examine your assumptions about what is necessary for God?
?
If knowledge is a necessary attribute of a knower, what implications does that have for your personal relationship with God? Do you seek to know Him through His creation while avoiding the trap of projecting creaturely limitations onto Him?
?
This passage guards against carelessly transferring properties from creation to the Creator. What attributes do you commonly use when describing God? Are you certain that these attributes are necessarily caused by His essence, not accidental? How can you train yourself to think more carefully about God's attributes?

Divine Transcendence
advanced
6 min
Direction Requires Another: God is Beyond Relation
Nasafi proves that direction cannot apply to God because it requires a relation to another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why direction cannot be attributed to God because it requires a counterpart, and God is self-subsistent without need of any other.

Core Idea
Direction needs a second; God is One and Self-Sufficient.

Having established the proper rule of transference, Nasafi now directly disproves direction for God. He argues that direction intrinsically requires another entity to relate to. Since God is self-subsistent and existed alone in pre-eternity, direction would have applied even then, which is absurd. He then analyzes the six directions to show each depends on an opposite, concluding that direction is only meaningful for limited beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and find the pre-eternity argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the reductio: if self-subsistence implied direction, God would have direction in pre-eternity alone.
2
Understand the analysis of six directions
Each direction (above, below, etc.) requires its opposite; direction is relational, not intrinsic.
This shows direction depends on otherness.
3
See the conditional about finiteness
If the opponent restricts the analogy to finite beings, Nasafi accepts but asks why they think God is finite.
Finiteness of God has been refuted.
4
Conclude the argument
Direction cannot apply to God because He has no counterpart and is not finite.
Connects to learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And [the] permissibility of that in the witnessed world – so why did you say that the evidence of distinction in our case does not exist? Rather it exists: it necessitates origination, which is impossible for the unseen, but permissible and even obligatory for the witnessed. Then we say to them: [the claim that] being under or above a direction is blame and deficiency is not conceded, for there is no deficiency in that nor elevation in highness of place, for how many a guard is above the roof and an emir in the house and a scout on elevated places and a sultan in low places. Then we say to them: every self-subsistent in the witnessed is a substance, and every substance is self-subsistent – do you then infer from that that the unseen is a substance? If they say: yes, then they have abandoned their doctrine and agreed with the Christians; and if they say: no, they have invalidated their evidence. Then we say to them: transference from the witnessed to the unseen is only obligatory when one of the two things is connected to the other with the connection of cause to effect, as in knowledge and the knower, and motion and the moving thing; and that does not rely merely on existence, but requires an additional condition, namely that it is impossible to attribute it to another. Do you not see that just as the knower is inseparable from knowledge and knowledge from the knower, it is impossible to attribute his being knowing to something beyond knowledge. So it is known that he was knowing because he has knowledge, so transference to the unseen is obligatory. But substantiality together with self-subsistence – if they are inseparable in the witnessed, but since it is not a substance because of its self-subsistence, but because it is a root from which the body is composed, the transference of its being a substance is not obligatory; rather the transference of its being self-subsistent is transitive. And when the matter is so, why did you say: the two of them in the witnessed exist, self-subsistent, because each one of them is in a direction from its companion, or each one of them is in the direction of its companion because they exist and are self-subsistent? Then we say to them: if they existed and were self-subsistent because each one of them is in a direction from its companion, then the existent self-subsistent would be in a direction even if there were no other with it, and the Creator, Exalted and High, would have been in a direction in pre-eternity because He was existent and self-subsistent – and this is impossible. For direction is only established by consideration of another. Do you not see that all directions are limited to six: above, below, behind, front, right, left; and each direction cannot be imagined to be established except by facing another; and the whole is composed of the individual; so when each individual direction cannot be imagined except between two, the rule of all direction is likewise, because of what has passed about obtaining knowledge of universals through the particular. And when the matter is so, attributing direction to existence and self-subsistence – while each of them is established by consideration of the self, not the other, and direction is only established by consideration of the other – is ignorance of realities. Then it is said to them: do you claim that self-subsistents are each in a direction from its companion absolutely, with the condition that each of them is limited and finite? If they say: absolutely – we do not concede; and what they adduce from the witnessed, both are limited and finite. And if they say: we say that with the condition that each of them is limited and finite – then it is conceded. But why do you say that the Creator is limited and finite? Moreover, we have already established proof of the impossibility of His being limited and finite. And God is the success.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument that attempts to prove that God has a direction (jiha) based on analogy (tamthil) from the witnessed world (shahid). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, presents several responses to this claim. First, he challenges the premise that direction implies deficiency, giving examples from everyday life where being above or below is not inherently deficient. Second, he questions the analogy by asking whether the opponent infers that God is a substance (jawhar) because all self-subsistent beings in the witnessed world are substances. If they say yes, they contradict their own doctrine and agree with Christians (who hold that God is a substance). If they say no, their analogy fails. Third, he explains the proper conditions for transference (ta'diya) from the witnessed to the unseen: it requires a necessary connection like cause and effect, not mere coexistence. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-dhat) does not necessarily entail direction, as direction requires another entity. Fourth, he argues that if self-subsistence implied direction, then God would have been in a direction in pre-eternity (before creation), which is impossible because direction presupposes a relation to something else. He then analyzes the nature of directions (above, below, etc.) showing that each requires a counterpart, so direction cannot be an intrinsic attribute of a self-subsistent being. Finally, he presents a conditional objection: if the opponent says the analogy holds only for limited and finite beings, then we concede but ask why they claim God is limited and finite, since that has been proven impossible.

Key Terms
جهة
محدود متناه
أزل
غير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think direction is an essential property of existence.
Correction: Direction requires another; existence and self-subsistence are intrinsic.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that God cannot have a direction in pre-eternity?
A) Because God was not yet self-subsistent.
B) Because direction requires another entity to relate to, and only God existed.
C) Because direction implies deficiency.
D) Because the six directions are limited.

Key Takeaway
Direction is relative and requires another; God is absolutely independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you find yourself 'facing' something other than God for approval, identity, or security? What would it mean to truly orient your heart toward God alone, as this lesson demands?
?
The passage teaches that direction requires a 'second.' Is there any 'second' in your life that you rely on as if it were a direction for your soul? How can you realign your trust so that God is your sole orientation?
?
When you perform acts of worship, is there any part of your intention that glances toward the recognition of others? Commit now to one specific prayer or action this week that you will do solely for God, with no other 'direction' in mind.

Refuting the Second Doubt: Creation Does Not Imply Direction
Nasafi presents and refutes the second doubt about creation implying direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the claim that God's creation of the world implies a direction for Him, by exposing the hidden belief in divine divisibility.

Core Idea
Direction for God implies divisibility, which is impossible.

Opponents argued that since God created the world, He must have a direction relative to it. Nasafi responds by showing that this argument secretly assumes God is divisible and has parts. This lesson examines his refutation and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt presented
Read the Arabic passage and translation to understand the opponents' question: Did God create the world within His essence or outside?
Notice how they frame the question to force a dichotomy.
2
Understand the opponents' reasoning
The opponents argue that whichever option is chosen, direction (jiha) is established. Identify why they think this follows.
They assume creation must be spatially related to the Creator.
3
See Nasafi's reply
Nasafi states that this question reveals their corrupt belief that God is divisible and partitioned (mutab'add mutajazzi), even if they outwardly deny it.
He connects the argument to the concept of body (jism) and self-subsistence (qiyam bi-dhat).
4
Recognise the underlying principle
The refutation shows that attributing direction to God entails attributing parts, which is impossible for the Creator. This reinforces divine transcendence.
This lesson connects to the broader Aqeedah principle that Allah is not confined by space or direction.

He notes that these opponents claim that by 'body' (jism) they mean 'self-subsistent' (qa'im bi-dhat), but the issue remains the same: their argument for direction implicitly attributes divisibility to God. The passage ends abruptly as the next page would continue the refutation.

Refuting Direction for Allah
Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that Allah is in a direction by showing direction requires relation and Allah is self-subsistent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing direction to Allah is impossible based on the relational nature of direction and Allah's self-subsistence.

Core Idea
Direction implies relation; Allah is self-subsistent and beyond relation.

Imam Nasafi begins by stating the impossibility of Allah being in a direction. He explains that direction only exists relative to another being, but Allah is self-subsistent (qa'im bidh-dhat). This lesson will guide you through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the dialectical exchange in the second half.
2
Understand the definition of direction
The passage explains that direction (jiha) is only established by relation to another. The six directions (above, below, etc.) are defined by opposition. This shows direction cannot be absolute.
3
Grasp the concept of self-subsistence
Allah is described as qa'im bidh-dhat (self-subsistent), meaning His existence is based on His own essence without reference to another. This contrasts with direction which requires relation.
4
Follow the dialectical argument
Nasafi presents two possible positions from opponents and refutes each, showing that either they accept finitude (which they cannot prove for Allah) or reject it (which is unreasonable).
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The argument concludes that attributing direction to Allah is 'ignorance of realities' and that Allah cannot be limited or finite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الأزل بجهة، لأنه كان موجودا قائما بالذات وهذا محال، إذ الجهة لا تثبت إلا باعتبار غير، ألا ترى أن الجهات كلها محصورة على الست وهي فوق وتحت وخلف وقدام وعن يمين وعن يسار، وكل جهة منها لن يتصور ثبوتها إلا بمقابلة غيرها، والكل يتركب من الفرد، فإذا كان كل فرد من الجهات لن يتصور إلا بين اثنين، فكان حكم كلية الجهات كذلك، لما مر من حصول المعرفة بالكليات بواسطة الجزئيات، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك كان تعليق الجهة بالوجود والقيام بالذات مع أن كل واحد منهما يثبت باعتبار النفس دون الغير، والجهة لا تثبت إلا باعتبار الغير جهلا بالحقائق. ثم يقال لهم: أتزعمون أن القائمين بالذات يكون كل واحد منهما بجهة من صاحبه على الإطلاق بشريطة كون كل واحد منهما محدودا متناهيا؟ فإن قالوا: على الإطلاق. فلا نسلم وما استدلوا به من الشاهد فهما محدودان متناهيان. وإن قالوا نقول ذلك بشريطة كون كل واحد منهما محدودا متناهيا. فمسلم. ولكن لم قلتم إن الباري محدد متناه؟ ثم إنا قد أقمنا الدلالة على استحالة كونه محدودا متناهيا، والله الموفق.
In pre-eternity (al-azal) He is with a direction, because He was existent and self-subsistent (qa'im bidh-dhat), and this is impossible, for direction is only established by relation to another. Do you not see that directions are all six: above and below, behind and front, right and left, and each direction cannot be conceived except in opposition to another, and the whole is composed of individuals; so if each individual of directions cannot be conceived except between two, then the ruling of all directions is likewise, because knowledge of universals is attained through particulars. And if this is the case, then attributing direction to existence and self-subsistence, while each of them is established by consideration of the self without the other, and direction is only established by consideration of the other, is ignorance of realities. Then it is said to them: Do you claim that two self-subsistent beings are each in a direction from the other absolutely, with the condition that each is limited and finite? If they say: absolutely, we do not accept, and what they adduce from the witnessed world are both limited and finite. And if they say: we say that with the condition that each is limited and finite, then it is accepted. But why do you say the Creator is limited and finite? Then we have established the proof of the impossibility of His being limited and finite. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah is in a direction (jiha). The author begins by stating that attributing direction to Allah is impossible because direction only exists in relation to another being, while Allah is self-subsistent (qa'im bidh-dhat). He then demonstrates that the six directions (above, below, behind, front, right, left) are each defined by opposition to another direction, so direction inherently implies relation. Since Allah's existence and self-subsistence are based on His own essence without reference to another, attaching direction to Him would be ignorance of realities. The author then engages in a dialectical exchange: if the opponent claims that two self-subsistent beings are each in a direction from the other absolutely, this is rejected because in the witnessed world such beings are limited and finite. If they qualify it with the condition that they are limited and finite, then the burden is on them to prove that the Creator is limited and finite, which is impossible as already proven.

Correction: This passage shows that direction inherently requires relation to another and implies finitude and limitation, which are incompatible with Allah's self-subsistence.

Key Takeaway
